            <b>
             External Links
            </b>
            <table class="roundy" style="background:#FFF; text-align:left;" width="100%">
             <tbody>
              <tr>
               <td>
                <ul>
                 <li>
                  <span class="plainlinks">
                   <a class="external text" href="https://www.smogon.com/dex/sv/pokemon/pecharunt/" rel="nofollow">
                    On Smogon Pokédex
                   </a>

        <p>
         <b>
          Pecharunt
         </b>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_Japanese_Pok%C3%A9mon_names" title="List of Japanese Pokémon names">
          Japanese
         </a>
         :
         <b>
          モモワロウ
         </b>
         <i>
          Momowarou
         </i>
         ) is a dual-type
         <a href="/wiki/Poison_(type)" title="Poison (type)">
          Poison
         </a>
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Ghost_(type)" title="Ghost (type)">
          Ghost
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Mythical_Pok%C3%A9mon" title="Mythical Pokémon">
          Mythical Pokémon
         </a>
         introduced during
         <a href="/wiki/Generation_IX" title="Generation IX">
          Generation IX
         </a>
         , in
         <a href="/wiki/The_Indigo_Disk" title="The Indigo Disk">
          The Indigo Disk
         </a>
         (though it was not made available until the release of
         <a href="/wiki/Mochi_Mayhem" title="Mochi Mayhem">
          Mochi Mayhem
         </a>
         ).
        </p>
        <p>
         It is not known to
         <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">
          evolve
         </a>
         into or from any other Pokémon.
        </p>
        <p>
         It is the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legendary_leader" title="Legendary leader">
          leader
         </a>
         of the
         <a href="/wiki/Loyal_Three" title="Loyal Three">
          Loyal Three
         </a>
         , and is associated with
         <a href="/wiki/Ogerpon_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Ogerpon (Pokémon)">
          Ogerpon
         </a>
         .
        </p>
        <div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation">
         <input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox">
          <div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en">
           <h2 id="mw-toc-heading">
            Contents
           </h2>

        <h2>
         <span class="mw-headline" id="Biology">
          Biology
         </span>
        </h2>
        <div class="thumb tleft">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1025Pecharunt_Dream_3.png">
           <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="350" decoding="async" height="175" loading="lazy" src="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/0/0f/1025Pecharunt_Dream_3.png/175px-1025Pecharunt_Dream_3.png" srcset="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/0/0f/1025Pecharunt_Dream_3.png/263px-1025Pecharunt_Dream_3.png 1.5x, https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/0/0f/1025Pecharunt_Dream_3.png 2x" width="175"/>
          </a>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1025Pecharunt_Dream_3.png" title="Enlarge">
            </a>
           </div>
           Pecharunt inside its shell
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <p>
         Pecharunt is a small Pokémon resembling a piece of
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/mochi" title="wp:mochi">
          mochi
         </a>
         . It has two forms it can take both inside and outside of battle. The first form resembles an upside-down peach, with a black circular face at the center and a thin, vertical line splitting its body into two halves. In its face are two white semicircle eyes, appearing to be frowning. It takes its second form upon opening up, revealing a smaller inner body resembling a peach's pit. It has a darker purple and pink body with two white eyes which are usually frowning, below which is a white, ribbon-shaped mouth. On its head rests two purple flaps and a scorpion-like ponytail. It has two heart-shaped paws at the bottom of its body, along with three black dots on each side underneath them. The discarded shell floats on both sides of Pecharunt, forming spiky wing-like appendages. The inside of these shells have a bright pink glow, outlined in black. The bright pink extends slightly through the black outline in six thin lines. The chains have a magenta color to them and are divided in identical segments, ending in a slightly larger segment with two protrusions, making it resemble the shape of Pecharunt's shell.
        </p>
        <p>
         According to the
         <a href="/wiki/Player_character" title="Player character">
          player
         </a>
         , Pecharunt smells incredibly sweet.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
         It is known to feign weakness by weeping, and acting like a baby in order to gain sympathy from others.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-website_2-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-website-2">
           [2]
          </a>
         </sup>
         If mortally wounded, Pecharunt will retreat into its shell and remain asleep for years so it can regain its strength. After being knocked out in
         <a href="/wiki/Kitakami" title="Kitakami">
          Kitakami
         </a>
         , it started being known as the "
         <b>
          Never-Rotting Peach
         </b>
         " due to its peach-like shell.
        </p>
        <div style="display: grid; grid-template-columns: 32px 1fr 32px; border: 1px solid #272727; background: #a0a0a0; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; max-width: 550px; border-radius: 60px; -moz-border-radius: 60px; -webkit-border-radius: 60px; -khtml-border-radius: 60px; -icab-border-radius: 60px; -o-border-radius: 60px;">
         <div style="background: #525252; border-radius: 60px; -moz-border-radius: 60px; -webkit-border-radius: 60px; -khtml-border-radius: 60px; -icab-border-radius: 60px; -o-border-radius: 60px;">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ani201ODEX.png" title="201">
           <img alt="201" data-file-height="32" data-file-width="32" decoding="async" height="32" loading="lazy" src="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/c/c4/Ani201ODEX.png" width="32"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div style="place-self: center; padding: 0 10px 0 10px;">
          <b>
           <a href="/wiki/Bulbapedia:Spoiler_warning" title="Bulbapedia:Spoiler warning">
            <span style="color: #272727">
             Spoiler warning:
            </span>
           </a>
          </b>
          this article may contain major plot or ending details.
         </div>
         <div style="background: #525252; border-radius: 60px; -moz-border-radius: 60px; -webkit-border-radius: 60px; -khtml-border-radius: 60px; -icab-border-radius: 60px; -o-border-radius: 60px;">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ani201ODEX.png" title="201">
           <img alt="201" data-file-height="32" data-file-width="32" decoding="async" height="32" loading="lazy" src="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/c/c4/Ani201ODEX.png" width="32"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="thumb tleft">
         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:126px;">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mdl_Carmine_Mochi.png">
           <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="124" decoding="async" height="240" loading="lazy" src="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/3/30/Mdl_Carmine_Mochi.png" width="124"/>
          </a>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <div class="magnify">
            <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mdl_Carmine_Mochi.png" title="Enlarge">
            </a>
           </div>
           <a href="/wiki/Carmine" title="Carmine">
            Carmine
           </a>
           under the effects of the Binding Mochi
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <p>
         Pecharunt stores poison in its peach-shaped shell and uses it to create
         <a href="/wiki/Toxic_Chain_(Ability)" title="Toxic Chain (Ability)">
          toxic chains
         </a>
         and roll up poisonous
         <a href="/wiki/Mochi" title="Mochi">
          Binding Mochi
         </a>
         , which are stored in its shell until they are needed. It is able to use
         <a href="/wiki/Malignant_Chain_(move)" title="Malignant Chain (move)">
          its toxic chains in combat
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Poison_(status_condition)" title="Poison (status condition)">
          badly poisoning
         </a>
         its enemies in the process. The chains are also capable of empowering other Pokémon, using its toxins to enhance certain aspects of their bodies, such as their muscles, brain, or looks, as seen with
         <a href="/wiki/Okidogi_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Okidogi (Pokémon)">
          Okidogi
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Munkidori_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Munkidori (Pokémon)">
          Munkidori
         </a>
         , and
         <a href="/wiki/Fezandipiti_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Fezandipiti (Pokémon)">
          Fezandipiti
         </a>
         , respectively. It serves its mochi to
         <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_(species)" title="Pokémon (species)">
          Pokémon
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">
          humans
         </a>
         , but may also shoot them at their mouths if necessary. According to
         <a href="/wiki/Penny" title="Penny">
          Penny
         </a>
         , the mochi that Pecharunt creates are somewhat sweet. The mochi draw out their deepest desires and powers, but the ones who eat it become chained to Pecharunt's will, as seen with its caretakers, who had their greed drawn out. In some cases, the ones that eat it may completely fall under its control, as seen with
         <a href="/wiki/Mossui_Town" title="Mossui Town">
          Mossui Town
         </a>
         's residents and the player's
         <a href="/wiki/Friend" title="Friend">
          friends
         </a>
         from
         <a href="/wiki/Paldea" title="Paldea">
          Paldea
         </a>
         .
        </p>
        <p>
         Humans under Pecharunt's control have purple eyes and are surrounded by a purple aura. The controlled humans also hold their arms while performing a chicken dance-like movement, repeating the word "mochi" constantly. However, in some cases, like with
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hideko" title="Hideko">
          Hideko
         </a>
         , it is shown that the possessed human can still speak somewhat freely, though it may simply be Pecharunt influencing the propagation of the mochi among humans. Humans under its influence are often still prone to innate emotion and desires —
         <a href="/wiki/Arven" title="Arven">
          Arven
         </a>
         is visibly embarrassed while dancing, Penny instinctively combines the word "mochi" with "Veevee", and
         <a href="/wiki/Nemona" title="Nemona">
          Nemona
         </a>
         still expresses a strong urge to battle, being able to morph "mochi" into "match". It can even command humans, and Pokémon to fight for it in battles, capable of controlling multiple creatures at once. It relies on others to fight for it due to its cowardly personality and size. However, Pecharunt will fight back if it is has no other option. Capturing Pecharunt will free those under its control with no memories of being controlled. The effect of Pecharunt's mochi on people are likened by
         <a href="/wiki/Kieran" title="Kieran">
          Kieran
         </a>
         to a curse.
        </p>
        <p>
         According to myth, Pecharunt came from a distant land where it was adopted by an elderly couple with no children. Pecharunt fed its adoptive parents Binding Mochi to secure their affection, which brought out their inner greed. They made many requests of Pecharunt, who gave them what they requested to be showered with further attention. The couple eventually asked for
         <a class="extiw" href="https://bulbapedia.bulbagarden.net/wiki/Category:Masks" title="en:Category:Masks">
          a brilliant set of masks
         </a>
         , which could only be found in Kitakami. Pecharunt left to obtain the masks, recruiting Okidogi, Munkidori, and Fezandipiti to aid in its quest. They successfully stole three masks from
         <a href="/wiki/Ogerpon_(game)" title="Ogerpon (game)">
          Ogerpon
         </a>
         , who defeated and slayed the Loyal Three in retaliation; Pecharunt only survived by going dormant within its shell. It would not surface found again until hundreds of years later when a
         <a href="/wiki/Mythical_Pecha_Berry" title="Mythical Pecha Berry">
          Mythical Pecha Berry
         </a>
         awoke it.
        </p>

            <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ani201ODEX.png" title="201">
             <img alt="201" data-file-height="32" data-file-width="32" decoding="async" height="32" loading="lazy" src="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/c/c4/Ani201ODEX.png" width="32"/>
            </a>
           </th>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>
        <p>
         Pecharunt is the
         <a href="/wiki/Signature_move" title="Signature move">
          only known Pokémon
         </a>
         capable of learning the move
         <a href="/wiki/Malignant_Chain_(move)" title="Malignant Chain (move)">
          Malignant Chain
         </a>
         . It is also the
         <a href="/wiki/Signature_Ability" title="Signature Ability">
          only known Pokémon
         </a>
         that can have
         <a href="/wiki/Poison_Puppeteer_(Ability)" title="Poison Puppeteer (Ability)">
          Poison Puppeteer
         </a>
         as an
         <a href="/wiki/Ability" title="Ability">
          Ability
         </a>
         .
        </p>

        <h2>
         <span class="mw-headline" id="Game_data">
          Game data
         </span>
        </h2>
        <div class="thumb tright">

        <h3>
         <span class="mw-headline" id="NPC_appearances">

         </span>

        <dl>
         <dd>

           </a>
          </i>
         </dd>
        </dl>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <b>
           <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_Scarlet_and_Violet" title="Pokémon Scarlet and Violet">
            Pokémon Scarlet and Violet
           </a>
           :
           <a href="/wiki/Mochi_Mayhem" title="Mochi Mayhem">
            Mochi Mayhem
           </a>
           :
           <a href="/wiki/Pecharunt_(game)" title="Pecharunt (game)">
            Pecharunt
           </a>
          </b>
          is a major character and a boss in the
          <a href="/wiki/The_Hidden_Treasure_of_Area_Zero" title="The Hidden Treasure of Area Zero">
           DLC
          </a>
          .
         </li>

               <td style="background:#FFFFFF; text-align:center; border:1px solid #D8D8D8;">
                5
               </td>
              </tr>
             </tbody>
            </table>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <td class="roundybottom" colspan="7" style="background:#A284A2; font-size: 90%; line-height:10px;">
            <ul>
             <li>
              <b>
               Bold
              </b>
              indicates a move that gets
              <a href="/wiki/Same-type_attack_bonus" title="Same-type attack bonus">
               <span style="color:#000;">
                STAB
               </span>
              </a>
              when used by Pecharunt
             </li>
             <li>
              <i>
               Italic
              </i>
              indicates a move that gets STAB only when used by an Evolution  of Pecharunt
             </li>
            </ul>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </tbody>
        </table>

         </span>
        </h2>

        <h2>
         <span class="mw-headline" id="Trivia">
          Trivia
         </span>
        </h2>
        <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="float:right">
         <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
          <div style="width: 155px">
           <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
            <div style="margin:28px auto;">
             <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pecharunt_Ogerpon_Backstory.png" title="A depiction of Pecharunt in Ogerpon's story">
              <img alt="A depiction of Pecharunt in Ogerpon's story" data-file-height="804" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="94" loading="lazy" src="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/3/3a/Pecharunt_Ogerpon_Backstory.png/120px-Pecharunt_Ogerpon_Backstory.png" srcset="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/3/3a/Pecharunt_Ogerpon_Backstory.png/180px-Pecharunt_Ogerpon_Backstory.png 1.5x, https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/3/3a/Pecharunt_Ogerpon_Backstory.png/240px-Pecharunt_Ogerpon_Backstory.png 2x" width="120"/>
             </a>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="gallerytext">
            <p>
             A depiction of Pecharunt in
             <a href="/wiki/Ogerpon_(game)" title="Ogerpon (game)">
              Ogerpon
             </a>
             's story
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>
         <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
          <div style="width: 155px">
           <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
            <div style="margin:26px auto;">
             <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loyal_Three_Sign_Image.png" title="The Loyal Three and a human child depicted on Kitakami signboards">
              <img alt="The Loyal Three and a human child depicted on Kitakami signboards" data-file-height="310" data-file-width="380" decoding="async" height="98" loading="lazy" src="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/4/41/Loyal_Three_Sign_Image.png/120px-Loyal_Three_Sign_Image.png" srcset="https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/4/41/Loyal_Three_Sign_Image.png/180px-Loyal_Three_Sign_Image.png 1.5x, https://archives.bulbagarden.net/media/upload/thumb/4/41/Loyal_Three_Sign_Image.png/240px-Loyal_Three_Sign_Image.png 2x" width="120"/>
             </a>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="gallerytext">
            <p>
             The
             <a href="/wiki/Loyal_Three" title="Loyal Three">
              Loyal Three
             </a>
             and a human child depicted on Kitakami signboards
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>
        </ul>
        <ul>
         <li>
          Before the official reveal of Pecharunt, it appeared with its shell closed in
          <a href="/wiki/Ogerpon_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Ogerpon (Pokémon)">
           Ogerpon
          </a>
          's story told by
          <a href="/wiki/Yukito_and_Hideko" title="Yukito and Hideko">
           Yukito
          </a>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_Scarlet_and_Violet" title="Pokémon Scarlet and Violet">
           Pokémon Scarlet and Violet
          </a>
          :
          <a href="/wiki/The_Teal_Mask" title="The Teal Mask">
           The Teal Mask
          </a>
          . What appears to be a Pecharunt doll can also be seen at Peachy's in
          <a href="/wiki/Mossui_Town" title="Mossui Town">
           Mossui Town
          </a>
          , which is later revealed in
          <a href="/wiki/Mochi_Mayhem" title="Mochi Mayhem">
           Mochi Mayhem
          </a>
          to be the actual Pecharunt, simply slumbering after the
          <a href="/wiki/Loyal_Three" title="Loyal Three">
           Loyal Three
          </a>
          's defeat at the hands of
          <a href="/wiki/Ogerpon_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Ogerpon (Pokémon)">
           Ogerpon
          </a>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          While its shell is closed, Pecharunt's shape is similar to the shape of the ends of the Loyal Three's toxic chains.
         </li>
         <li>
          The signboards that tell the legends of Kitakami show an image depicting a human child chasing a large monstrous ogre alongside the Loyal Three. While a lady in
          <a href="/wiki/Kitakami_Hall" title="Kitakami Hall">
           Kitakami Hall
          </a>
          ponders if this child was their trainer, it is likely instead a reference to or even a depiction of Pecharunt leading the trio.
         </li>
         <li>
          Pecharunt is known internally as
          <i>
           Dokutaro
          </i>
          , a reference to its basis on the tale of
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Momotar%C5%8D" title="wp:Momotarō">
           Momotarō
          </a>
          and its
          <a href="/wiki/Poison_(type)" title="Poison (type)">
           Poison
          </a>
          type (
          <i>
           doku
          </i>
          is Japanese for "poison").
         </li>
         <li>
          Pecharunt is the only
          <a href="/wiki/Mythical_Pok%C3%A9mon" title="Mythical Pokémon">
           Mythical Pokémon
          </a>
          :
          <ul>
           <li>
            That is Poison type, excluding
            <a href="/wiki/Arceus_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Arceus (Pokémon)">
             Arceus
            </a>
            while holding a
            <a href="/wiki/Toxic_Plate" title="Toxic Plate">
             Toxic Plate
            </a>
            .
           </li>
           <li>
            To have been introduced in
            <a href="/wiki/Generation_IX" title="Generation IX">
             Generation IX
            </a>
            .
           </li>
           <li>
            Whose English name is different from its Japanese name.
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          Pecharunt is the lightest Mythical Pokémon.
         </li>
         <li>
          Pecharunt has the highest base
          <a href="/wiki/Stat#Defense" title="Stat">
           Defense
          </a>
          stat of all
          <a href="/wiki/Ghost_(type)" title="Ghost (type)">
           Ghost-type
          </a>
          Pokémon.
         </li>
         <li>
          Pecharunt, like the
          <a href="/wiki/Loyal_Three" title="Loyal Three">
           Loyal Three
          </a>
          , seems to share a thematic tie to the number
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/8" title="wp:8">
           eight
          </a>
          . This may be because the character
          <i>
           8
          </i>
          looks like a set of chains, reflecting its
          <a href="/wiki/Signature_move" title="Signature move">
           signature move
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Malignant_Chain_(move)" title="Malignant Chain (move)">
           Malignant Chain
          </a>
          . It may also be because eight is considered a lucky number in many Asian cultures, including Japanese, which aligns with the trio's naming convention and role. Additionally, 88 can be read in Japanese as
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_wordplay#Goroawase" title="wp:Japanese wordplay">
           goroawase
          </a>
          for やばい
          <i>
           yabai
          </i>
          , which can mean "terrible" or "dangerous", referencing its true malevolent nature. It can also be read as goroawase for ぱちぱち
          <i>
           pachipachi
          </i>
          , the sound of clapping, referencing the outer shell it hides in closing around its body.
          <ul>
           <li>
            All of its
            <a href="/wiki/Base_stats" title="Base stats">
             base stats
            </a>
            are 88, except for Defense, which is 160, a multiple of 8.
           </li>
           <li>
            At the end of Mochi Mayhem, Pecharunt can be caught at level 88.
           </li>
           <li>
            All of the levels it learns moves at, aside from level 1, are multiples of 8. The same is also true for the Loyal Three.
           </li>
           <li>
            There are 8 complete chains Pecharunt uses to bind the Loyal Three: Okidogi has three in its scarf, Munkidori has one in its headband, and Fezandipiti has four in its belt.
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          Pecharunt,
          <a href="/wiki/Walking_Wake_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Walking Wake (Pokémon)">
           Walking Wake
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="/wiki/Iron_Leaves_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Iron Leaves (Pokémon)">
           Iron Leaves
          </a>
          are the only Pokémon that can be registered but are not required for the completion of the Blueberry Pokédex.
          <ul>
           <li>
            In addition, Pecharunt is the only Pokémon with this distinction that is not a
            <a href="/wiki/Paradox_Pok%C3%A9mon" title="Paradox Pokémon">
             Paradox Pokémon
            </a>
            , instead being a Mythical Pokémon.
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          Pecharunt and
          <a href="/wiki/Meltan_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Meltan (Pokémon)">
           Meltan
          </a>
          are the only Mythical Pokémon to have never been made available in a
          <a href="/wiki/Cherish_Ball" title="Cherish Ball">
           Cherish Ball
          </a>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          During the final battle in Mochi Mayhem, Pecharunt either is the recipient of or subject to special reactions depending on whether the player has
          <a href="/wiki/Ogerpon_(game)" title="Ogerpon (game)">
           Ogerpon
          </a>
          and/or any of the Loyal Three members in their party and uses them against it.
          <ul>
           <li>
            If the player uses Ogerpon against it, a scene will play where Ogerpon shows visible distress and anger and yells "GRAH! Pon PON!!!", alluding to Pecharunt's actions against Ogerpon and her companion in the past.
           </li>
           <li>
            If the player uses any of the Loyal Three against it, a scene will play where Pecharunt reacts with visible shock and anger before yelling "Pechaaa! Chraaahhh!", likely due to the Loyal Three turning against it. It should be noted that the scene replays with each member when they are first used against it.
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
        <h3>
         <span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">
          Origin
         </span>
        </h3>
        <p>
         Pecharunt, together with
         <a href="/wiki/Okidogi_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Okidogi (Pokémon)">
          Okidogi
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Munkidori_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Munkidori (Pokémon)">
          Munkidori
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Fezandipiti_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Fezandipiti (Pokémon)">
          Fezandipiti
         </a>
         , and
         <a href="/wiki/Ogerpon_(Pok%C3%A9mon)" title="Ogerpon (Pokémon)">
          Ogerpon
         </a>
         , may reference the Japanese folktale of
         <i>
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Momotar%C5%8D" title="wp:Momotarō">
           Momotarō
          </a>
         </i>
         . The tale relates the titular Momotarō, a boy born from inside a peach, who traveled alongside a talking dog, monkey, and pheasant to fight a band of
         <i>
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/oni" title="wp:oni">
           oni
          </a>
         </i>
         (a Japanese folkloric creature commonly equated to ogres in translations). Pecharunt appears to represent Momotarō himself, visually and in its lore. Pecharunt's appearance resembles popular depictions of Momotarō with the headband and tied hair. Its outer shell resembles a bisected peach or
         <a href="/wiki/Pecha_Berry" title="Pecha Berry">
          Pecha Berry
         </a>
         , referencing how Momotarō was found as a baby inside a cut peach.
        </p>
        <p>
         Pecharunt's story also mirrors that of Momotarō. Pecharunt was raised by two elderly people, went on an adventure to a distant land, teamed up with a dog, monkey, and pheasant, and fought an oni. However, the ending of Pecharunt's story is the opposite to that of Momotarō's, with the group being beaten by the oni. Pecharunt's habit of feeding others poisonous mochi is likely based on how Momotarō recruited his companions by feeding them
         <i>
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kibi_dango_(millet_dumpling)" title="wp:Kibi dango (millet dumpling)">
           kibi dango
          </a>
         </i>
         , a type of mochi.
        </p>
        <p>
         Pecharunt's small stature and its peach-shaped shell also make it resemble a peach pit. Its
         <a href="/wiki/Poison_(type)" title="Poison (type)">
          Poison
         </a>
         type may refer to the fact that the peach pit contains chemicals that are toxic in large doses. It may also reference the
         <a href="/wiki/Pecha_Berry" title="Pecha Berry">
          Pecha Berry
         </a>
         's effect of curing poison. Its
         <a href="/wiki/Ghost_(type)" title="Ghost (type)">
          Ghost
         </a>
         type could reference the
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shintoist" title="wp:Shintoist">
          Shintoist
         </a>
         myth of the creator deity
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Izanagi-no-Mikoto" title="wp:Izanagi-no-Mikoto">
          Izanagi-no-Mikoto
         </a>
         's descent to
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yomi" title="wp:Yomi">
          Yomi
         </a>
         (the Shintoist underworld), in which Izanagi threw three peaches to drive off his pursuers and escape the land of the dead, later declaring the peach a divine fruit. Given its moniker of "Never-Rotting Peach", Pecharunt could also be based on the
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peaches_of_Immortality" title="wp:Peaches of Immortality">
          Peaches of Immortality
         </a>
         in Chinese mythology, which confer great longevity to their consumers. Its habit of acting like a baby to gain the sympathy of people is similar to the behavior of certain
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/y%C5%8Dkai" title="wp:yōkai">
          yōkai
         </a>
         like the
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konaki-jiji" title="wp:Konaki-jiji">
          Konaki-jiji
         </a>
         . Pecharunt may also draw inspiration from the
         <i>
          <a class="extiw" href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E4%BA%BA%E5%BD%A2%E7%A5%9E" title="jwp:人形神">
           hinnagami
          </a>
         </i>
         , a doll-shaped yōkai that will grant its owner's wishes but will always demand more and more requests, and that will possess their owner until their death. Pecharunt's myth shows how its adoptive family became greedier over time, and the Loyal Three are all said to have had a wish granted by Pecharunt.
         <i>
          Hinnagami
         </i>
         are built using soil from a graveyard, which could also contribute to Pecharunt's Ghost type.
        </p>
        <p>
         The yellowish coloration of Pecharunt's
         <a href="/wiki/Shiny_Pok%C3%A9mon" title="Shiny Pokémon">
          Shiny
         </a>
         form resembles the flesh of some peach varieties.
        </p>
        <h4>
         <span class="mw-headline" id="Name_origin">
          Name origin
         </span>
        </h4>
        <p>
         Pecharunt may be a combination of
         <i>
          peach
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Pecha_Berry" title="Pecha Berry">
           Pecha Berry
          </a>
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          runt
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          petulant
         </i>
         .
        </p>
        <p>
         Momowarou may be a combination of 桃太郎
         <i>
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Momotar%C5%8D" title="wp:Momotarō">
           Momotarō
          </a>
         </i>
         , 桃
         <i>
          momo
         </i>
         (peach), and 悪し
         <i>
          waroshi
         </i>
         (bad or inferior; the classical Japanese form of 悪い
         <i>
          warui
         </i>
         ) or 和郎
         <i>
          warō
         </i>
         (boy).
        </p>

        // Initialize elements
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-left-s", wAbove: 1520, wBelow: 1699, hAbove: 700});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-left-m", wAbove: 1700, wBelow: 1890, hAbove: 700});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-left-l", wAbove: 1891, hAbove: 700});

appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-right-s", wAbove: 945, wBelow: 1099, hAbove: 964});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-right-m", wAbove: 1100, wBelow: 1399, hAbove: 964});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-right-l", wAbove: 1400, hAbove: 964});
appendElementIf({id: "adthrive-right-rect", hBelow: 964});


// Appends element if condition is met
function appendElementIf({id, wAbove, wBelow, hAbove, hBelow}) {

	// find browser height
	var w = window.innerWidth;
	var h = window.innerHeight;

	// If true after browser size check then unit is added
	var condition = true;

	// Check size conditions
	if (wBelow && (w > wBelow)) condition = false;
	if (wAbove && (w < wAbove)) condition = false;

	if (hBelow && (h > hBelow)) condition = false;
	if (hAbove && (h < hAbove)) condition = false;

	// Append element if condition is met
	if (condition) {
		createAndAppendElement(id);
	}
}


// creates and appends a div element to the body
function createAndAppendElement(id)
{
	var atEl = document.createElement('div');
	atEl.id = id;
	document.body.appendChild(atEl);
}
